‚ĚĮ I don't get why ruby is needed? I can just see the portfolio site on          
  wazihyeaser.github.io? Why is it needed? Answer shortly.                      

‚óŹ You're right that you don't need it to view the site. GitHub Actions already
  runs Ruby in the cloud, builds your Jekyll source into HTML, and publishes
  that ‚ÄĒ which is why wazihyeaser.github.io works fine.

  Ruby locally is only needed to preview changes before pushing. Without it, the
  loop is: edit ‚Üí commit ‚Üí push ‚Üí wait ~1‚Äď2 min for CI ‚Üí look at the live site
  ‚Üí repeat. Every experiment is public, and a broken build means a broken live
  site until you fix it.

  For an overhaul touching layout, icons, and every page, that's a painful way
  to iterate. Not a blocker ‚ÄĒ just slow and risky.

  Worth noting: this cost disappears entirely if you migrate off Jekyll, since
  Node is already installed and npm run dev would give you instant local
  preview. But that's the design discussion you've parked, so it can wait.

‚óŹ Both are client-rendered React SPAs, not academic templates ‚ÄĒ that's the core
  difference.

  Their stacks
  - anik81 ‚ÄĒ Vite + React, 402 KB JS bundle, 463-byte HTML shell. Nav: Home /
  About / Research / Projects / Contact.
  - sawradip ‚ÄĒ single-page anchor-scroll site, footer credits "Designed by
  Brittany Chiang" (the widely-forked brittanychiang.com dev-portfolio design).
  Sections: Hero ‚Üí About ‚Üí Publications ‚Üí Achievements ‚Üí Education ‚Üí Experience
  ‚Üí Contact.

  What they do that yours doesn't

  1. One page, anchor-scrolled. No hunting through 7 nav items. Sawradip's whole
  story is one downward scroll. Yours splits thin content across
  blog/publications/projects/repositories/CV/teaching/submenus ‚ÄĒ which makes
  each page look emptier than it is.
  2. A hero with a claim. "I create intelligence." Yours opens with a job-title
  subtitle. A hero line is the single highest-leverage fix on your site.
  3. Achievements as a first-class section. Sawradip leads with GSoC, Robi
  Datathon, IEEE VIP Cup ‚ÄĒ rank stated up front. You have real wins buried in
  resume.json and nothing on the site.
  4. Tabbed experience. Company selector on the left, role details on the right.
  Compact, dense, senior-feeling.
  5. Publications as cards with citation counts ‚ÄĒ not a bibliography dump.
  6. Text-forward, minimal icons. Icons only for social links. Directly
  addresses your icon complaint.

  My suggestion for you

  Go the anik81 direction ‚ÄĒ Vite + React, since you're leaning that way and Node
  is already installed. But borrow sawradip's structure: a single scrolling
  home page (Hero ‚Üí About ‚Üí Research ‚Üí Publications ‚Üí Achievements ‚Üí Experience
  ‚Üí Contact), with Publications and Projects as the only separate pages once
  they outgrow the scroll.

  Two honest cautions:
  - A 402 KB JS bundle to render mostly text is wasteful, and client-rendered 
  SPAs are weak for SEO ‚ÄĒ search engines and Google Scholar see an empty shell.
  For an academic site meant to be found by your name, that matters. Astro gives
  you the same React components and design freedom but ships static HTML. Same
  look, better fundamentals.
  - Don't fork Brittany Chiang's design directly. It's forked thousands of times
  ‚ÄĒ you'd be trading one recognizable template for another, which is the exact
  problem you're trying to escape.

‚ĚĮ These are some valid points:                                                  
                                                                                
  Two honest cautions:                                                          
  - A 402 KB JS bundle to render mostly text is wasteful, and client-rendered   
  SPAs are weak for SEO ‚ÄĒ search engines and Google Scholar see an empty shell. 
  For an academic site meant to be found by your name, that matters. Astro      
  gives you the same React components and design freedom but ships static HTML. 
  Same look, better fundamentals.                                               
  - Don't fork Brittany Chiang's design directly. It's forked thousands of      
  times ‚ÄĒ you'd be trading one recognizable template for another, which is the  
  exact problem you're trying to escape.                                        
  Can you explain a bit more so that I can take better decision.                
  Answer shortly.                                                               

‚óŹ 1. The "empty shell" problem ‚ÄĒ concretely

  anik81's entire homepage HTML is 463 bytes. I grepped it: no name, no
  publication titles, no description, no Open Graph tags. Everything is painted
  in by 402 KB of JavaScript after the browser loads.

  Who never runs that JavaScript:
  - Google Scholar's crawler. It doesn't execute JS. It looks for citation_title
  / citation_author meta tags in raw HTML. A React SPA is invisible to it ‚ÄĒ
  which matters a lot for an academic profile.
  - LinkedIn, X, WhatsApp link previews. They fetch raw HTML only. Share
  anik81's link and you get a blank card with a bare URL. Share a static site
  and you get your photo, name, and tagline.
  - LLM crawlers (the thing increasingly answering "who is Wazih Yeaser
  Tanzim?").

  Googlebot does render JS, but on a delayed second pass ‚ÄĒ slower and less
  reliable than static HTML. For a site whose whole job is being found by your
  name, you're taking a real penalty for zero benefit, since your content is
  text that never changes after build.

  Astro fixes this without changing how you build. You write the same React
  components; Astro renders them to HTML at build time and ships 0 KB of JS by 
  default. You opt into interactivity only where you need it (a theme toggle, a
  filter). Same design freedom, same component model, static output.

  2. The template-recognition problem

  Brittany Chiang's design isn't a subtle influence ‚ÄĒ it's a look: navy #0a192f
  background, teal #64ffda accent, numbered section headings (01. About Me),
  tabbed experience panel, oversized hero line. It's one of the most-forked
  portfolio designs on GitHub. Anyone in CS/EE has seen it dozens of times.

  So: al-folio is instantly recognizable to academics. Brittany Chiang is
  instantly recognizable to engineers. Your reviewers are both. Swapping one for
  the other doesn't fix "looks like a template."

  The distinction that matters: their structure ‚ÄĒ hero with a claim,
  achievements up front, tabbed experience, publication cards with citation
  counts ‚ÄĒ is generic, good, and worth taking. Their visual layer ‚ÄĒ color, type,
  spacing, section-numbering ‚ÄĒ is the recognizable part. Take the first, build
  your own version of the second.

  Net recommendation: Astro + Tailwind, sawradip's structure, your own visual
  identity.

‚úĽ Baked for 25s

‚ĚĮ I don't want to use single page structure. Yes, I don't have as much to fill  
  up all the subpage, but I don't need to immediately, I will fill those one by 
  one gradually. I am just trying to my phd journey so obviously it will not    
  be filled up at very beginning. But having subpage structure help me to have  
  a more professional look and to have options for the future.                  
  And, How much of a change will I see if I use astro+tailwind? Answer shortly. 

‚óŹ On multi-page ‚ÄĒ agreed, and your reasoning is sound. A structure you grow into
  beats one you outgrow. The only rule I'd hold you to: ship a page when it has
  content, not before. A page with two solid entries reads as early-career; a
  page with a heading and nothing under it reads as abandoned. Keep the routes
  planned, add them to the nav as they fill.

  How much change from Astro + Tailwind ‚ÄĒ honestly: none by itself.

  The framework isn't the improvement. A fresh Astro site looks like plain HTML.
  Nothing about Astro or Tailwind makes a site look professional.

  What they actually give you is permission:

  - Right now you cannot change your icon size. There's no config key, and the
  CSS lives in a gem your CI gate forbids you from overriding. That's not a hard
  problem ‚ÄĒ it's a locked door.
  - With Astro + Tailwind, every value ‚ÄĒ type scale, spacing, color, icon size,
  card layout ‚ÄĒ is a line you edit directly, previewed instantly with npm run 
  dev.

  So the split is roughly:

  - ~0% of the visual improvement comes from the framework
  - ~100% comes from design decisions ‚ÄĒ typography, spacing, hierarchy,
  restraint
  - but ~100% of those decisions are currently blocked, and Astro unblocks them

  The secondary wins are real but quieter: static HTML for Scholar and link
  previews, no Ruby, fast local iteration, content stays Markdown.

  One caution: migrating and not investing in the design work would leave you
  with a site that's technically better and visually no different. The stack is
  the prerequisite, not the fix.

  Want me to log these two decisions ‚ÄĒ multi-page confirmed, Astro leaning ‚ÄĒ
  into project-notes/PROJECT.md?

  I never installed Ruby ‚ÄĒ fetching the live site's compiled CSS gave me better
  data than gem source would have, since it's the final computed output.

  What I matched exactly: every --global-* variable in both themes (magenta
  #b509ac light, blue #2698ba dark), Roboto 300, the 930px container, 57px
  navbar, the float-right profile photo at 30%, the publication badge/Abs/Bib

  the data-theme + data-theme-setting + localStorage system‚Üílight‚Üídark cycle.

  Content carried over verbatim ‚ÄĒ about paragraphs, 3 news items, 4 publications
  with abstracts and the thesis BibTeX, 4 projects, the full CV (still reads
  resume.json). I rewrote nothing.

  Five deliberate deviations, all of which you can veto:

  1. Your projects page currently renders empty on the live site.
  _pages/projects.md declares display_categories: [work, fun], but all four
  projects use category: research ‚ÄĒ nothing matches, so both grids are blank.
  Live .card count is 0; the port renders 4. This is the one place I chose
  fixing over faithfulness, because porting a blank page seemed worse.
  2. Blog posts not carried over. The 31 posts are al-folio tutorials ("a post

‚óŹ Two options, since Ruby isn't installed:

  Docker (no Ruby needed):
  docker compose up -d
  ‚Üí http://127.0.0.1:8080/ (your baseurl is "", so no /al-folio suffix). Stop

  (https://rubyinstaller.org/)):
  bundle install
  bundle exec jekyll serve
  ‚Üí http://localhost:4000/

  Docker is the faster path right now. One caveat: it serves from
  container-local /tmp/_site and watches _config.yml for changes, so config
  edits restart Jekyll automatically ‚ÄĒ but the first up builds the image and
  will take a few minutes.

‚óŹ Build is running. One real problem surfaced, and it's a classic Windows trap:

  Imagemagick: Command returned exit 4 with error Invalid Parameter - /Codes

  ImageMagick isn't installed, so convert is resolving to Windows' built-in
  C:\Windows\System32\convert.exe ‚ÄĒ the NTFS filesystem conversion utility. It's
  parsing F:/Codes/... and rejecting /Codes as an invalid flag. All 69
  responsive .webp files silently failed despite the "Generated 69 file(s)"
  line.

  Not fatal ‚ÄĒ al-folio's <img onerror> strips the broken srcset and falls back
  to the original JPEGs, so the site will look right. But it's noise on every
  build.

  Let me wait for the server to actually come up before touching anything.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ While that finishes ‚ÄĒ you'll want ImageMagick installed regardless, since your
  CI installs it and generates those WebP files in production:

  winget install ImageMagick.ImageMagick

  (New terminal afterward, as before.) The alternative is setting
  imagemagick.enabled: false in _config.yml, but that would disable responsive
  images on the live site too, not just locally ‚ÄĒ so installing is the better
  fix.

  I'll report as soon as the server binds.

  Three things worth knowing:

  1. Deleting a page is just deleting the file ‚ÄĒ _pages/teaching.md,
  _pages/dropdown.md (that's "submenus"), _pages/books.md,
  _pages/repositories.md. Nav order is the nav_order: number in each file's
  front matter.
  2. ImageMagick is still missing ‚ÄĒ WebP variants fail silently, images fall
  back to JPEG. Fix with winget install ImageMagick.ImageMagick whenever
  convenient.
  3. The icon-size fix (item¬†8) is still blocked on this stack ‚ÄĒ it lives in the
  gem, and test/style_contract.js:64 forbids the _sass/ override that would fix
  it. Everything else on your list is editable right now.

  The server runs in the background; tell me when you want it stopped. What do
  you want to tackle first?

‚úĽ Worked for 15s

‚ĚĮ I have already done this: winget install ImageMagick.ImageMagick, but still   
  the error is showing.                                                         
  What can I do? Answer in 3 lines.                                             

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ ImageMagick 7 installed fine, but it only ships magick.exe ‚ÄĒ it dropped the
  legacy convert.exe, so convert still resolves to Windows' NTFS tool.

  Fix: create a shim so convert means ImageMagick ‚ÄĒ in an admin PowerShell, run
  cmd /c mklink "C:\Program Files\ImageMagick-7.1.2-Q16-HDRI\convert.exe" 
  "C:\Program Files\ImageMagick-7.1.2-Q16-HDRI\magick.exe", then open a new
  terminal and confirm convert -version prints ImageMagick.

  Simpler alternative if you'd rather not touch system paths: set imagemagick: 
  enabled: false in _config.yml for local work ‚ÄĒ CI still generates the WebP
  files on deploy.

‚úĽ Cogitated for 22s

! cmd /c mklink "C:\Program Files\ImageMagick-7.1.2-Q16-HDRI\convert.exe"       
  "C:\Program Files\ImageMagick-7.1.2-Q16-HDRI\magick.exe"                      
  ‚éŅ ¬†Microsoft Windows [Version 10.0.26200.8875]
     (c) Microsoft Corporation. All rights reserved.

     F:\Codes\wazihyeaser.github.io>

  Ran 2 shell commands (ctrl+o to expand)
‚óŹ Good news ‚ÄĒ ImageMagick is at PATH index 0, ahead of System32, so a
  convert.exe there will win. The mklink never actually executed (cmd opened
  interactively instead).

  Run this in an Administrator PowerShell ‚ÄĒ a plain copy works, since magick.exe
  switches to legacy mode when invoked under the name convert:

  Copy-Item "C:\Program Files\ImageMagick-7.1.2-Q16-HDRI\magick.exe" "C:\Program
  Files\ImageMagick-7.1.2-Q16-HDRI\convert.exe"

  Then open a new terminal and check convert -version prints ImageMagick rather
  than the NTFS tool, and restart Jekyll.

  If you'd rather not run anything as admin, set imagemagick: enabled: false in
  _config.yml instead ‚ÄĒ local builds get faster and CI still generates the WebP
  files on deploy.

‚ĚĮ Now, I want to update the content of the home page. There are several changes 
  I want to make:

  to be much smaller, an standard size used according to the web developement

  2. Wazih Yeaser Tanzim - only Wazih is bold, I want to change the font of     
  "Wazih Yeaser Tanzim" use an eye chatching font and also either use bold for  
  all three words or don't use bold.                                            
  3. Remove the news sections and selected publications section. Replcae that   
  with featured section. In these featured sections, there will be section from 
  different subpages for say I will add one significant research work or one    
  great projects or a popular blog here, it will be horizontally scrollable and 
  a small tag will show on the content, showing that content is from which      
  part, like for blog it will have that tag showing blog and that tag will be   
  clickable and clicking it will take to the blog subpage.                      
  Now, this also can be that for different subpage, each will have one

  be implemented or if you have better suggestions, please share. No code

‚óŹ Good ‚ÄĒ this is worth thinking through carefully, because two of the three
  touch gem-owned rendering, and the featured section has a real design trap in
  it (horizontal scroll with too few items). Let me lay out how each works, then
  the options and my recommendation. No changes made yet.

  First, the constraint that shapes everything: the homepage is rendered by the
  about layout inside the al_folio_core gem ‚ÄĒ the name markup, the social row,
  the news and "selected publications" blocks are all emitted there, and I can't
  edit that file in this repo (the CI gate forbids _layouts//_sass/ overrides).
  But I don't need to. All three of your asks can be done from about.md alone ‚ÄĒ
  front-matter flags to remove sections, a scoped inline <style> block to
  restyle, and Liquid in the page body to build the featured section. Nothing
  gem-level, nothing that trips CI, fully reversible, and it ports cleanly to
  Astro later.

  ---
  1. Social icons ‚Üí standard size

  The cause is one gem rule: .social .contact-icons { font-size: 4rem } ‚ÄĒ that's
  64px, roughly 3√ó a normal inline social icon. They're icon fonts, so they
  inherit that size, and the row has no real gap (spacing comes from whitespace
  at 64px, which is why they look sparse).

  Web-standard inline social icons are 20‚Äď24px. I'd set the container to
  font-size: 1.5rem (24px) and make it a flex row with gap: 0.9rem so spacing is
  deliberate, not accidental. Done via a scoped <style> in about.md ‚ÄĒ it only
  outputs on the homepage, which is the only page the social row appears on, so
  there's no bleed. Purgecss won't strip it (it only cleans CSS files, not
  inline blocks).

  One decision: 24px (classic, understated) or 28px (a touch more presence)? I
  lean 24px.

  ---
  2. Name ‚ÄĒ font + weight

  Current markup: <span class="font-weight-bold">Wazih</span> Yeaser Tanzim ‚ÄĒ
  the bold-on-first-word is hardcoded in the gem layout. I can't remove the
  span, but I can neutralize it with CSS (.post-title .font-weight-bold { 
  font-weight: inherit }) and set a new font + uniform weight on .post-title.
  Also inline <style>, no gem edit.

  Weight: uniform across all three words ‚ÄĒ I'd go 500 (medium) or 600 
  (semibold), not bold. Uniform reads more deliberate than one bold word.

  Font ‚ÄĒ your body text is Roboto (sans), so a display serif for the name 
  creates strong, classic contrast. Three good directions:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā    Font     ‚Ēā                     Feel                     ‚Ēā    Cost    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā Characterful old-style serif ‚ÄĒ distinctive,  ‚Ēā +1 line in ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā Fraunces    ‚Ēā modern-academic, "eye-catching" without      ‚Ēā  config    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā shouting                                     ‚Ēā            ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Playfair    ‚Ēā High-contrast elegant serif ‚ÄĒ striking,      ‚Ēā +1 line    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā Display     ‚Ēā classic, slightly common                     ‚Ēā            ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Space       ‚Ēā Techy geometric sans ‚ÄĒ fits the ML/6G        ‚Ēā +1 line    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā Grotesk     ‚Ēā engineering identity; stays sans             ‚Ēā            ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Roboto Slab ‚Ēā Slab serif, already loaded on your site ‚ÄĒ    ‚Ēā free       ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā solid, zero new request                      ‚Ēā            ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  My pick: Fraunces if you want it to feel crafted and stand out, Space Grotesk
  if you want it to feel technical/modern. Adding one is a single line in
  _config.yml's Google-Fonts URL (config change ‚Üí needs a server restart).
  Roboto Slab is the zero-cost fallback if you'd rather not add a request.

  ---
  3. The Featured section ‚ÄĒ the real design question

  Removing news + selected-publications is trivial: announcements.enabled: false
  and selected_papers: false in about.md. The featured section then goes in the
  page body.

  Here's where I want to push back a little and give you a better shape than
  pure horizontal scroll.

  The trap: horizontal scroll only earns its keep when a row overflows ‚ÄĒ roughly
  4+ cards. Right now you have ~1 item per category (and Blog has no real posts
  yet ‚ÄĒ only al-folio demo posts). A horizontal scroller showing 1‚Äď2 cards
  looks broken: there's nothing to scroll, and the scroll affordance implies
  content that isn't there. Horizontal scroll also has weak discoverability on
  desktop (people don't expect to scroll sideways).

  So the honest question is which of two structures fits, and I'd build either
  to degrade gracefully ‚ÄĒ a flex strip with overflow-x: auto + CSS scroll-snap
  that simply displays 1‚Äď3 cards inline and only starts scrolling once there are
  enough. That gives you "horizontally scrollable" for the future without
  looking empty today.

  Layout A ‚ÄĒ one mixed "Featured" strip. A single row; each card carries a
  clickable source tag (Research / Project / Blog) that links to its subpage.
  This is closest to your original description and the tags do real work
  (they're the only source label). Best when you feature 3‚Äď6 hand-picked items
  total.

  Layout B ‚ÄĒ one strip per category. Three rows: Research ‚Üí Projects ‚Üí Writing,
  each a horizontal scroll-snap strip with a header and a "View all ‚Üí" link.
  Clearer narrative for a PhD-seeking portfolio (leads with research). But here
  the row header already names the category, so the per-card tag becomes
  redundant.

  My recommendation: Layout A now, evolve to B later. With your current volume,
  one curated "Featured" strip of 3 cards (one research, one project, one blog
  placeholder), each with a clickable tag, looks intentional and does exactly
  what you described. When any category grows past ~4 items, we split that
  category into its own row (Layout B). This also makes the tags meaningful from
  day one.

  How items get "featured" ‚ÄĒ the data model. Two options:

  - Curated _data/featured.yml (my pick): a hand-written list where each entry
  is { type, title, blurb, image, link }. Full editorial control over what leads
  and in what order, handles all content types uniformly ‚ÄĒ crucially including
  publications, which live in papers.bib and are painful to render as cards
  otherwise. Downside: you maintain the featured entry separately from the
  source. For a homepage highlight reel, curating by hand is appropriate ‚ÄĒ you
  want to choose exactly what leads.
  - featured: true flags on each project/post: no duplication, auto-pulled via
  Liquid. But it can't include bib publications, and ties each card to whatever
  front matter that collection happens to have.

  I recommend _data/featured.yml ‚ÄĒ it's the only clean way to feature a
  publication alongside a project and a post, and curation is the right instinct
  for a front page.

  Tag design: a small pill on each card, theme-colored, uppercase (RESEARCH),
  wrapped in an <a> to /publications/, /projects/, /blog/. To keep the whole
  card clickable and the tag separately clickable, the card links to the item
  and the tag links to the section (nested-link handling is straightforward).

  UX niceties I'd include: scroll-snap so cards align; a subtle fade at the
  right edge to hint "more ‚Üí" when it overflows; keyboard-accessible and
  aria-labelled scroll region. Optional (needs a little JS): arrow buttons for
  desktop.

  One caveat to flag now: the Blog featured card has no real content ‚ÄĒ your
  posts are still the 31 al-folio demos. So that slot is a placeholder until you
  write a real post. Options: (a) leave a "Writing ‚ÄĒ coming soon" card, (b)
  omit Blog from featured until you have a post, or (c) feature something else
  in that third slot for now.

  ---
  What I need you to confirm before I build

  1. Social size: 24px (my pick) or 28px?
  2. Name font: Fraunces / Playfair / Space Grotesk / Roboto Slab (free) ‚ÄĒ and
  weight 500 or 600?
  3. Featured layout: one mixed tagged strip (A, my pick) or per-category rows
  (B)?
  4. Featured data: curated _data/featured.yml (my pick) or featured: true
  flags?
  5. Blog slot: placeholder card, omit for now, or feature something else there?

  Once you pick, I'll implement it all in about.md (+ _data/featured.yml), and
  you'll see it live on refresh ‚ÄĒ the only restart needed is if you choose to
  add a new font (config change).

‚óŹ Good set of changes. Three are clean; one (the navbar) bumps into the gem
  boundary, so let me be precise about each before touching anything. No changes
  made yet.

  1. Image right / writing left, remove location+email, tighten the copy

  Feasibility: The image is already on the right (profile.align: right,
  floated). What's actually happening now is the text wraps under the image,
  which reads as messy rather than a clean two-column. So the real improvements
  here are:

  - Remove "Dhaka, Bangladesh" + email under the image ‚Üí that's the more_info
  block in about.md front matter. Clean deletion. You lose nothing: your email
  stays reachable via the social row (moving up per point¬†2) and the Contact
  page.
  - Clean two-column ‚Üí I'll make the text sit in its own left column beside the
  image instead of wrapping under it. Minimal CSS, no gem edit.
  - Tighter copy ‚Üí your current 4 paragraphs are long for a hero. Your subtitle
  already states your roles, so the body shouldn't repeat them ‚ÄĒ it should go
  straight to substance. Draft for your approval:

  ‚Ėé I develop machine-learning methods for the wireless physical layer, 
  ‚Ėé replacing classical iterative precoding and beamforming with deep-unrolled 
  ‚Ėé and physics-informed models that keep the structure ‚ÄĒ and reliability ‚ÄĒ of 
  ‚Ėé the optimizers they learn from. My current focus is max-min-fair precoding 
  ‚Ėé for cell-free massive MIMO, with broader interests spanning RIS, near-field 
  ‚Ėé and terahertz communication, ISAC, and 6G systems. I completed my B.Sc. in 
  ‚Ėé EEE at BUET in 2024 and am seeking PhD opportunities.

  Three sentences, formal, no title-repetition. Edit freely or tell me the tone
  to shift.

  2. Social icons under the writing

  Feasibility: clean. The theme renders social at the page bottom via the
  social: flag. I'll turn that off and render the same row inside the left text 
  column, right under your intro. One improvement: when it moves into a
  left-aligned column, the icons should be left-aligned too (not centered as
  they are now) ‚ÄĒ centered icons under left text looks off. I'd also drop the 
  "Email is the best way to reach me" note, since the email icon sits right
  there. Confirm dropping it.

  3. Featured headings match page names

  Trivial ‚ÄĒ just the heading: values in _data/featured.yml. To match your nav
  exactly: "Research & Publications", "Projects", "Blog". Two small confirms:
  you wrote "Blogs" but your nav says Blog (singular) ‚ÄĒ which do you want? And
  "&" (matches nav) or the spelled-out "and"? I recommend matching the nav
  verbatim.

  4. Center the navbar ‚ÄĒ the one real snag

  This is different from the others: the navbar appears on every page, so
  centering it needs site-wide CSS. My inline-<style>-in-about.md trick only
  reaches the homepage ‚ÄĒ it can't restyle the navbar on Projects, Blog, etc. And
  al-folio's navbar CSS lives in the gem, with no config option for alignment.
  So the options are:

  - (a) Per-page inline style ‚ÄĒ drop the same tiny centering rule into each of
  your 5 page files. Works site-wide today, no gem/CI involvement, fully
  reversible. Slight duplication, but it's ~4 lines and goes away at migration.
  My recommendation for now.
  - (b) Proper site-wide custom stylesheet ‚ÄĒ cleaner, but requires
  relaxing/removing the style_contract CI check (which only exists to protect
  the upstream al-folio starter ‚ÄĒ irrelevant to your personal fork). Bigger
  decision.
  - (c) Defer to the Astro migration ‚ÄĒ where centering is literally one line,
  site-wide by nature.

  One design nuance: on subpages your name shows as the left brand, so centered
  nav will center in the space beside the brand, not the full viewport (true
  viewport-centering needs absolute positioning and can look detached). On the
  homepage there's no brand, so it centers perfectly. I'd go with the standard
  "center in available space" ‚ÄĒ it looks right on home and fine on subpages.

‚óŹ Good batch. I fetched anik81's bundle and checked your photo ‚ÄĒ two findings
  shape the discussion: anik81's contact page is a working form ("Get In Touch"
  ‚Üí message field ‚Üí "Send Message"), and your prof_pic.jpg is square 
  (1200√ó1169), not a tall portrait. Both matter below. Here's my read on each,
  with recommendations. No changes made yet.

  1. Remove the name from subpage navbars

  Easy ‚ÄĒ I'll hide the navbar brand site-wide. Note: it's actually rendered on
  the left, not right (my grid puts it there); you may be seeing a stale view.
  Either way it goes. Bonus: with no brand on any page, the nav centers
  perfectly everywhere and the grid logic gets simpler. ‚úÖ no concerns.

  2. The name font

  I did change it ‚ÄĒ to Fraunces, which you chose two turns ago. If it looks
  wrong right now, it's almost certainly because the font never loaded: Fraunces
  was added to _config.yml, and config changes need a server restart (Ctrl+C ‚Üí
  bundle exec jekyll serve). Without that, it falls back to Georgia ‚ÄĒ a generic
  serif that looks off. So the fix is either: (a) restart and keep Fraunces, or
  (b) revert the name to the theme's default (Roboto). Since the whole hero is
  being redesigned (point 5), I'd fold this in ‚ÄĒ tell me which font you want on
  the new greeting.

  3. Remove the email blink

  Agreed, it reads as gimmicky. I'll delete the animation entirely. ‚úÖ

  4 & 5. New hero (the sketch) + larger image

  The sketch is a real restructure, so I'd build the hero in the page body for
  full control (hide the theme's default header + image, render my own):
  - Centered greeting on top ‚ÄĒ "Hi," / This is Wazih Yeaser Tanzim / roles line.
  - Row below: large image left, description (your bio) right, vertically
  centered.
  - Social icons centered underneath (your "Logo" pill).
  - Featured strips below that.

  Two things to flag:
  - Your photo is square, so it'll render as a large square or circle ‚ÄĒ not the
  tall portrait the sketch draws (that's just a placeholder shape). A true tall
  portrait would need a different photo. I'd recommend a large circle (clean,
  modern, matches sites like anik81) or a large rounded square. Which?
  - Greeting wording: the sketch says "ML Engineer @Shottify," but your CV/site
  says "AI Engineer @ Shottify." I'd keep it consistent with your CV. Also,
  "This is Wazih‚Ä¶" is a touch casual for a PhD portfolio ‚ÄĒ "Hi, I'm Wazih‚Ä¶"
  reads more natural. Your call on both.

  6. Contact page like anik81

  anik81's is a contact form ‚ÄĒ and here's the catch: GitHub Pages is static, so
  a form can't email you on its own. It needs a third-party handler. Two honest
  paths:
  - (a) Real form (matches anik81): via Web3Forms (free, no account beyond an
  email-verified access key ‚ÄĒ easiest for static) or Formspree (free 50/mo,
  needs an account). You POST to their endpoint; they email you submissions. I'd
  need you to sign up and give me the key.
  - (b) Contact section, no form: a clean page with your email, LinkedIn,
  GitHub, and an "Email me" button. Zero dependencies, zero spam, nothing to
  maintain ‚ÄĒ and honestly, most academic/PhD portfolios do this, since
  committees just want to email you directly.

  My recommendation: (b) for an academic site. But if you specifically want the
  form feel, (a) with Web3Forms. Which?

  7. "Nothing yet" instead of "Coming soon"

  Trivial ‚ÄĒ the empty featured card will read "Nothing yet." ‚úÖ

‚óŹ Here's my rewrite. I kept every fact from your draft but tightened the
  grammar, sequencing, and register so it reads like confident, native academic
  prose. I'll flag two accuracy points and a couple of options rather than
  silently deciding them.

  Recommended (three short paragraphs)

  ‚Ėé I am a research assistant at BUET, where I develop machine-learning methods 
  ‚Ėé for the wireless physical layer ‚ÄĒ most recently, learned precoders for 
  ‚Ėé cell-free massive MIMO. My undergraduate thesis introduced a 
  ‚Ėé deep-learning-aided hybrid beamformer for multi-user MIMO terahertz 
  ‚Ėé communication.
  ‚Ėé
  ‚Ėé My research interests span cell-free MIMO, beamforming, reconfigurable 
  ‚Ėé intelligent surfaces (RIS), integrated sensing and communication (ISAC), 
  ‚Ėé holographic MIMO, and fast solvers for the convex and non-convex 
  ‚Ėé optimization problems that recur across wireless systems. I am always glad 
  ‚Ėé to discuss research collaboration.
  ‚Ėé
  ‚Ėé Alongside my research, I work as an ML Engineer at Shottify, where I use 
  ‚Ėé large language models to build automated pipelines that analyze multimodal 
  ‚Ėé web content ‚ÄĒ interpreting its context, intent, and tone ‚ÄĒ to measure how 
  ‚Ėé relevant it is to a given interest.

  Tighter alternative (two paragraphs ‚ÄĒ often reads more confident in a hero)

  ‚Ėé I am a research assistant at BUET developing machine-learning methods for 
  ‚Ėé the wireless physical layer: learned precoders for cell-free massive MIMO, 
  ‚Ėé and ‚ÄĒ in my undergraduate thesis ‚ÄĒ a deep-learning-aided hybrid beamformer 
  ‚Ėé for multi-user MIMO terahertz systems. My interests span cell-free MIMO, 
  ‚Ėé beamforming, RIS, ISAC, holographic MIMO, and fast solvers for convex and 
  ‚Ėé non-convex optimization in wireless systems; I am always glad to discuss 
  ‚Ėé collaboration.
  ‚Ėé
  ‚Ėé Alongside my research, I work as an ML Engineer at Shottify, using large 
  ‚Ėé language models to analyze multimodal web content ‚ÄĒ its context, intent, and
  ‚Ėé tone ‚ÄĒ and measure how relevant it is to a given interest.

  What I changed and why

  - Grammar/idiom fixes: "specializing to" ‚Üí "in"; "undergraduation" ‚Üí
  "undergraduate"; "relevancy of a content" ‚Üí "relevance of content"; "fast
  solving ‚Ä¶ optimization problem" ‚Üí "fast solvers for ‚Ä¶ optimization problems."
  - Active, single-tense voice: present tense for current roles; past for the
  thesis. Your draft mixed "I have worked / I have used," which reads slightly
  non-native ‚ÄĒ the fix is consistent tense.
  - Dropped a redundancy: RIS and IRS are the same idea, so I kept just RIS.
  - "holographic beamforming" ‚Üí "holographic MIMO" (the more standard term). Say
  the word if you prefer your original.

  Two things to confirm before I apply it

  1. THz vs. cell-free ‚ÄĒ accuracy check. Your draft merges them ("intelligent
  precoder for cell-free MIMO for THz"), but your CV has them as separate
  threads: your RA work is cell-free massive MIMO (max-min-fair, DeepMIMO 28
  GHz), and THz is your thesis (MU-MIMO hybrid beamforming). I separated them
  above, which is the safer, more credible framing for a committee. If your RA 
  work genuinely is THz cell-free, tell me and I'll merge them back.
  2. Should the hero say you're seeking a PhD? Your draft dropped it. Given the
  whole site is aimed at admissions, I'd add a short closing clause ‚ÄĒ e.g. "‚Ä¶and
  am currently seeking PhD positions." Want that in, or keep it to the Contact
  page only?

  Optional: I can also fold in your real technical signature ‚ÄĒ "deep-unrolled 
  and physics-informed" precoders ‚ÄĒ which is more distinctive than "learned

‚ĚĮ Now, in the change theme, button, there is three theme I guess. CHeck and     
  tell me what are they? I want to keep two themes. Night mode and normal.

‚óŹ Yes ‚ÄĒ the toggle cycles through three states (I confirmed this from the theme
  JS earlier):

  1. System ‚ÄĒ follows your device/OS setting automatically (the half sun-moon
  icon).
  2. Light ‚ÄĒ forced light mode (the sun icon).
  3. Dark ‚ÄĒ forced dark mode (the moon icon).

  It goes System ‚Üí Light ‚Üí Dark ‚Üí System on each click.

  To keep just two, I'd remove "System", leaving Light (your "normal") and Dark 
  (night mode) ‚ÄĒ the button would then just toggle straight between those two.

  One small note for when you want it done: the toggle logic lives in the
  theme's gem JavaScript, not in this repo, so dropping the System state needs a
  small custom script override on the pages (same inline approach we've used
  for CSS) ‚ÄĒ not a config flag. Say the word and I'll implement it.

‚úĽ Cogitated for 10s
‚ĚĮ Implement it ‚ÄĒ remove the system theme, keep light and dark.                  

‚óŹ Implementing. The toggle logic is in the theme gem, so I'll inject a small
  site-wide script (via the footer, which renders on every page) that locks the
  theme to a concrete light/dark and replaces the three-state cycle with a
  straight light‚ÜĒdark toggle ‚ÄĒ while preserving the theme's dark-mode fixups for
  tables and code highlighting.

      25 +      var s = localStorage.getItem('theme');                   
      26 +      if (s !== 'light' && s !== 'dark') {                     
      27 +        s = window.matchMedia('(prefers-color-scheme: dark)').m
         +atches ? 'dark' : 'light';                                     
      28 +      }                                                        
      29 +      localStorage.setItem('theme', s);                        
      30 +      html.setAttribute('data-theme', s);                      
      31 +      html.setAttribute('data-theme-setting', s);              
      32 +      function sideEffects(t) {                                
      33 +        var lh = document.getElementById('highlight_theme_light
         +');                                                            
      34 +        var dh = document.getElementById('highlight_theme_dark'

         +) { tb.classList.toggle('table-dark', t === 'dark'); });

         +) ? 'dark' : 'light';

      57 +      } else {

      59 +      }

‚óŹ Done ‚ÄĒ the script rendered intact and is on every page (via the footer).

  What it does: on load it converts any "system" (or unset) preference into a
  concrete Light or Dark ‚ÄĒ resolving to your OS preference on first visit, then
  locking it ‚ÄĒ and replaces the theme's three-state cycle with a straight Light 
  ‚ÜĒ Dark toggle. So the button now flips directly between the two: sun icon in
  dark mode, moon icon in light mode; the half-sun-moon "system" state never
  appears. It also keeps the theme's dark-mode fixups for tables and code blocks
  so nothing breaks in dark mode.

  Restart required ‚ÄĒ it's a _config.yml change: Ctrl+C ‚Üí bundle exec jekyll 
  serve. After that, click the toggle a few times to confirm it only swaps
  Light/Dark.

  If you had previously left it on "system," your first load after restart will
  pick whichever matches your OS, then stay two-state from there.

‚úĽ Worked for 2m 52s

‚ĚĮ About the external sources, So, if I have medium account and write there, I   
  can just add that post here? Answer in 2 lines. No code changes.              

‚óŹ Yes ‚ÄĒ external_sources can pull your Medium posts automatically: add your feed
  (rss_url: https://medium.com/feed/@your-username) and every Medium article
  shows up on your blog as a card linking back to Medium. You can also list
  one-off external URLs manually instead of a whole feed.

  Two caveats: it fetches at build time (a new Medium post only appears after
  the next site rebuild/deploy), and the cards link out to Medium rather than
  hosting the text on your site.

  use? Answer in 3 lines.                                                       
  No code chages.                                                               

‚óŹ It's not a fixed list ‚ÄĒ external_sources accepts any RSS/Atom feed or a manual
  list of URLs. So common picks: Substack, WordPress, Dev.to, Hashnode,
  LinkedIn newsletters, a YouTube channel feed, or even an arXiv author feed.

  "Medium" and "Google Blog" were just examples ‚ÄĒ the first form is rss_url:
  (auto-pulls a feed), the second is a hand-listed posts: array (any one-off
  links).

  Given your goals, an arXiv author feed or a Substack would be the most
  on-brand ones to surface here.

‚óŹ Done ‚ÄĒ the blog page is now card-based. Refresh (no restart; these are
  page/post edits):

  - Cards: each post is a card ‚ÄĒ thumbnail, title, description, and a clean meta
  line "2026 ¬∑ Self-help ¬∑ 5 min read". The whole card links to the post.
  - Category bar at top: pills auto-derived from the categories actually used
  across your posts ‚ÄĒ right now All ¬∑ Self-help. Add a post with categories: 
  academia (or any new one) and that pill appears automatically, no editing the
  blog page.
  - Filtering: clicking a pill instantly shows/hides matching cards
  (client-side, no reload); an empty category shows a "Nothing here yet"
  message.
  - The turtle post is now categorized self-help.

  Two things worth knowing:
  1. Multi-word categories (like "book review") are a Jekyll gotcha ‚ÄĒ written
  plainly, categories: book review becomes two categories ("book" + "review").
  To keep it as one, use either categories: [book review] (YAML list) or a
  hyphen: categories: book-review (displays as "Book-review"). Tell me which
  convention you prefer and I'll note it.
  2. It looks a little sparse with one card, but it's built to fill out as you
  add posts.

‚óŹ Here's the audit. The root cause is that everything we've built are CSS 
  patches layered on top of the al-folio theme ‚ÄĒ the base is unchanged, so the
  new custom pieces (Fraunces hero, cards) sit on an old foundation. Concretely:

  1. The colour palette is still 100% al-folio. The accent is their magenta
  #b509ac (light) / teal-blue #2698ba (dark) ‚ÄĒ you chose a font (Fraunces) but
  never a palette. Every link, active nav item, filter pill, button, badge,
  "View all ‚Üí", card-hover, and the scroll progress bar uses that magenta. This
  is almost certainly the loudest "not aligned" thing. It's also the al-folio
  signature colour, so the site still reads as "an al-folio site."

  2. Typography is split. Fraunces is applied only to the hero name and the
  featured/blog strip titles. Every real page title ‚ÄĒ "Blog", "Projects",
  "Research & Publications" ‚ÄĒ is still al-folio's Roboto 300 (thin). So the
  homepage feels bespoke and the subpages feel default. Body text everywhere is
  thin Roboto (the defining al-folio look).

  3. The footer is a fixed dark bar. It's fixed-bottom (glued to the viewport,
  can overlap content on short pages) with a dark background even in light mode,
  at tiny 0.75rem text. We reorganised its contents, but structurally it's
  still the al-folio footer ‚ÄĒ a dark strip under a light, airy design.

  4. Three different card styles. Featured (.fcard), blog (.blog-card), and
  projects (al-folio .card ‚ÄĒ 2rem title, a hardcoded grey #747373 that doesn't
  even adapt to dark mode). Same concept, three looks.

  5. Publications uses the al-folio bibliography style ‚ÄĒ coloured badge, dashed
  author underline, outlined Abs/Bib buttons ‚ÄĒ a different visual language from
  the cards everywhere else.

  6. Five orphaned pages are still live with old demo styling and placeholder
  content, hidden from the nav but publicly reachable (and Google-indexable):
  /repositories/ (torvalds, Bootstrap), /teaching/ (Prof. Example), /books/ (The
  Godfather), /cv/, /news/.

  ---
  The honest framing: items 1‚Äď5 exist because we're patching al-folio instead of
  owning the design. Fixing them cohesively means either (a) more overrides ‚ÄĒ
  define a real palette, apply Fraunces (or your chosen display face) to all
  titles, restyle the footer, unify the cards ‚ÄĒ all doable with our inline
  approach but it's more scaffolding on a foundation you'll eventually replace;
  or (b) the Astro migration we discussed, where one design system covers
  everything and there are no fallbacks to fight.

  Cheapest immediate win, independent of that choice: delete the five orphaned
  pages (#6) ‚ÄĒ pure placeholder junk that's currently indexable.

  Want me to (1) just delete the orphaned pages now, (2) do a round of overrides
  to unify palette + typography + footer + cards on al-folio, or (3) treat this
  as the trigger to plan the Astro migration?

  I'm an electrical and electronic engineer by training and a researcher by     
  inclination, based in Dhaka, Bangladesh. I completed my B.Sc. at BUET in      
  2024, and since then my work has settled at the meeting point of two fields I 
  find hard to keep apart: wireless communication and machine learning.         
                                                                                
  What draws me to that intersection is a specific tension. The classical tools 
  of the physical layer ‚ÄĒ the iterative optimizers behind precoding and         
  beamforming ‚ÄĒ are dependable but slow, and they scale badly as networks grow. 
  Purely data-driven replacements are fast, but they throw away the structure   
  that made those methods trustworthy in the first place. Most of my research   
  is an attempt to keep both at once: deep-learning models that inherit the     
  shape of the optimizers they learn from, applied to cell-free massive MIMO    
  and terahertz systems.                                                        
                                                                                
  I currently split my time between research and industry ‚ÄĒ a research          
  assistantship at CASR, BUET, and an ML engineering role at Shottify ‚ÄĒ while   
  preparing my first manuscripts and looking for a PhD position where I can     
  take these questions further. Away from the work, I read widely and write the 
  occasional essay; a few of them live on this site.

  Research-interest verification (what you asked me to check). Most of your list
  is solid, but there are real issues:

  ‚ö† Fix before you publish these ‚ÄĒ they'll read as errors to a committee:
  1. You listed "Hybrid Pinching-Fluid Antenna Systems (HPFAS)" twice ‚ÄĒ I
  removed the duplicate.
  2. "HPFAS" is not an established term. Pinching antennas (PASS
  (https://arxiv.org/abs/2501.10753)) and fluid/movable antennas (FAS
  (https://arxiv.org/html/2412.03839v1)) are both real, current 6G topics ‚ÄĒ but
  the literature treats them as distinct technologies under the umbrella
  "flexible/reconfigurable antennas," never combined as "HPFAS." ‚Üí Recommend
  splitting into "Pinching-Antenna Systems (PASS)" and "Fluid & Movable Antenna 
  Systems."
  3. "NGRA" is not a recognized acronym. "Reconfigurable antennas for next-gen
  networks" is a real area (survey (https://arxiv.org/pdf/2606.12139)), but the
  acronym is invented. ‚Üí Use "Reconfigurable Antennas (RAs)" or
  "Electromagnetically Reconfigurable Antennas (ERAs)."
  4. "Deep Edge Learning" isn't standard ‚ÄĒ the established term is Federated 
  Edge Learning (FEEL) (IEEE (https://ieeexplore.ieee.org/document/9861221/)). ‚Üí
  Recommend "Federated & Edge Learning for Wireless Communication."
  5. Redundant pair: "Near-Field Terahertz Communications" and "THz & Sub-THz
  Communication Systems" overlap ‚Üí merge into "Near-Field & (Sub-)Terahertz 
  Communications."

  Everything else checks out (cell-free, beamforming, RIS, ISAC, holographic
  MIMO, ultra-massive MIMO, 6G).

‚ĚĮ What is semantic communication? Answer shortly.                               

‚óŹ Semantic communication is a shift in what a wireless system actually
  transmits: instead of reproducing the exact bits/waveform a sender emitted
  (Shannon's classical goal), it transmits only the meaning relevant to the
  receiver's task ‚ÄĒ and the receiver reconstructs intent, not raw data.

  A quick example: rather than sending every pixel of a video, the system
  extracts and sends "person walking left, red car behind" ‚ÄĒ whatever the
  receiver needs to act on. Typically a neural encoder at the transmitter and
  decoder at the receiver are trained jointly to preserve meaning over the
  channel.

  Why it matters for 6G: it can slash bandwidth and is robust to noise (a few
  corrupted bits don't matter if the meaning survives). It's especially suited
  to task-oriented links ‚ÄĒ machine-to-machine, autonomous systems, AR/VR ‚ÄĒ where
  the goal is a correct action, not a bit-perfect copy.

  The catch: "meaning" is task- and context-dependent, so defining and measuring
  semantic fidelity (vs. Shannon's clean bit-error rate) is still an open
  research problem ‚ÄĒ which is part of why it's an active area.

‚úĽ Churned for 10s

  interest in your CV (resume.json), not in your thesis, publications, or
  projects, which are all cell-free massive MIMO, beamforming, THz, and
  deep-unrolling.

  So it's an "area I'm interested in," not "something I've done." Keep it in
  interests only if you genuinely want to pursue it; otherwise drop it to avoid
  a committee asking about work that isn't there.

‚óŹ Good material ‚ÄĒ the substance is strong (especially the CASR bullets, which
  finally show concrete contributions). The main issues are grammar, parallel
  structure, and a bit of repetition. Here's my evaluation with polished
  rewrites. No code changes yet.

  Cross-cutting fixes

  - Verb-led + parallel: every bullet should start with a strong verb (Built,
  Designed, Benchmarked, Reproduced), not a noun phrase ("A thorough Study‚Ä¶",
  "An automated system‚Ä¶").
  - Tense per role: present for ongoing (Shottify), past for finished (CASR
  sub-projects, BrimAI, Dr. Lutfa).
  - Terminology: use "cell-free massive MIMO" (not "Cell-free MIMO"),
  "physics-inspired" (hyphen). Typos: differnet, physcis.
  - "modified novel loss function" is contradictory ‚ÄĒ either you modified an 
  existing one or designed a novel one. I assumed designed a novel.

  Shottify ‚ÄĒ ML Engineer (present tense; I reordered to follow the pipeline)

  - Build an automated system that fetches relevant multimodal content from
  multiple platforms.
  - Build LLM pipelines that analyze that content ‚ÄĒ reading its context, intent,
  and tone.
  - Measure how relevant a given piece of content is to a specified interest, at
  scale.
  - Build a personalized CMS that performs complex database operations over the
  analyzed, verified content.

  CASR ‚ÄĒ Research Assistant (your strongest set; polished, de-repeated)

  - Built a physics-inspired, deep-unrolled precoder for digital beamforming in
  cell-free massive MIMO, and benchmarked it against methods from the
  literature.
  - Built a DL-aided hybrid beamformer with a novel unsupervised loss function,
  and compared it against existing approaches.
  - Built a federated-learning hybrid beamformer robust to imperfect CSI, with a
  novel physics-inspired, channel-aware aggregation scheme.

  Dr. Lutfa Akter ‚ÄĒ Research Assistant (honest, but study-heavy)

  Your four bullets all describe reviewing/studying ‚ÄĒ reviewers value
  contribution over "studied X." I'd tighten to three verb-led lines and lead
  with the concrete deliverable (reproduction):
  - Reproduced results from multiple benchmark cell-free massive MIMO papers to
  establish reliable baselines.
  - Benchmarked and compared digital beamforming algorithms for cell-free
  massive MIMO.
  - Reviewed datasets and the deep-learning / federated-learning literature,
  mapping current trends and open problems.

  Comment: keeping all four is fine, but three of yours (study / dataset
  analysis / trends review) overlap heavily ‚ÄĒ trimming reads stronger. Your
  call.

  Ordering

  Your current order is already reverse-chronological by start date ‚ÄĒ CASR (Jun
  2025) ‚Üí Shottify (May 2025) ‚Üí BrimAI (Feb 2025) ‚Üí Dr. Lutfa (Nov 2024) ‚ÄĒ which
  is standard CV convention. One judgment call: Shottify is your only ongoing
  role, so some prefer it first. Want CASR first (by start date, as now) or the 
  ongoing Shottify role first?

  ---Confirm the wording (mine or yours) and the ordering, and I'll apply it.

‚óŹ This is a solid direction ‚ÄĒ two honest buckets (published vs in-progress) is
  exactly right for where your work is, and keeping it .bib-driven is the smart
  call. Let me evaluate the whole thing, flag a few real risks, and lay out what
  I'd confirm before building. No code yet.

  How it'll work mechanically

  - Two sections, still .bib-driven: I'd use two bib files ‚ÄĒ papers.bib (‚Üí
  Publications) and a new ongoing.bib (‚Üí Ongoing Research). You drop an entry in
  the right file and it appears in the right section. Clean and matches your
  "add by bib" wish.
  - The card design in that image can't come from al-folio's default
  bibliography markup (it has no "type pill / venue-link pill / Read More"). To
  get it and keep .bib, I'd add a custom bibliography template that renders each
  entry as that card. That's the one piece that touches a gem-owned layout ‚ÄĒ a
  cosmetic CI-check flag, irrelevant to your fork and gone at migration. It's
  the right tradeoff to keep both the look and the .bib workflow.
  - "One horizontal strip" = full-width cards, one per row, stacked (not
  2-across like the image). Good ‚ÄĒ better for reading abstracts.

  The one design change I'd push back on

  The image is anik81's palette ‚ÄĒ cyan/purple on near-black, monospace. If I
  copy that literally, this page will clash with everything else you've built
  (magenta accent, light default, Fraunces). I strongly recommend taking the
  layout (pills, doc icon, "Abstract:", Read More) but rendering it in your
  design tokens so it matches the site. Mono pills actually fit ‚ÄĒ you already
  use mono for the timeline dates and labels.

  Suggestions & cautions

  1. ‚ö† Be careful uploading "rough" manuscripts to arXiv. arXiv is permanent
  (you can supersede but not delete), moderated, and timestamps priority ‚ÄĒ a
  half-finished draft can hurt with a committee. Safer options for the Ongoing
  links: a GitHub repo, a clean 1‚Äď2 page extended abstract, or ResearchGate
  (softer), or just show status only ("Manuscript in preparation") with no link
  until it's genuinely ready. Don't feel obligated to attach a link to every
  ongoing item.
  2. Empty-state: you're clearing everything, and most of your work is
  in-progress ‚ÄĒ so Publications may start empty. I'll add a graceful "No
  publications yet" line instead of a blank section.
  3. Link redundancy: the image has three links to (likely) the same paper ‚ÄĒ doc
  icon, venue pill, and Read More. I'd consolidate: venue pill ‚Üí the paper,
  drop or repurpose the doc icon (‚Üí PDF), Read More ‚Üí abstract/detail. Cleaner.
  4. Truncate the abstract (~3 lines, line-clamped) so cards stay compact; full
  text on click/Read More.
  5. Show authors (your name bolded) ‚ÄĒ standard academic signal, and the image
  omits it.

  Confirm before I build

  1. Design: match your site's tokens (rec) or copy anik81's cyan/purple
  exactly?
  2. Ongoing links: are you OK starting with status-only / GitHub rather than
  rough arXiv PDFs (rec), or do you definitely want a PDF link slot on every

  3. Clearing entries: fully empty both files, or should I pre-sort your

‚óŹ Good calls overall. Let me comment on each, with a few refinements.

  1. The "not added yet" link

  This is the one I'd change. A link that lands on a "not added yet" page is a 
  dead end ‚ÄĒ a visitor (or committee member) clicks and hits nothing, which
  reads as unfinished, the opposite of what you want. Cleaner: make the pill a
  non-clickable status label ("Manuscript in preparation," "Preprint ‚ÄĒ soon")
  that automatically becomes a live link the moment you put a URL in the bib 
  entry. Same end state, no dead-end page, and it reads as intentional until
  then. I'd strongly recommend this over a placeholder page ‚ÄĒ but I'll do
  either.

  2. The conference paper & Google Scholar

  Small but important: you don't need Google Scholar to list the paper. Scholar
  is a separate citation profile; your site's Publications comes straight from
  papers.bib. So you can add the conference paper to the site today ‚ÄĒ just give
  me title, authors, venue, year, and a link/DOI, and I'll format the bib entry.
  Treat the Scholar profile as an independent, later task (and when you have
  the Scholar ID, I'll switch the hidden Scholar icon back on across the site).
  Don't block Publications on it.

  3. Dropping the doc icon + Read More / detail pages

  - Doc icon gone ‚ÄĒ agreed, purely decorative.
  - Omitting per-paper detail pages is fine for now, but I'd flag it as a
  "later" asset: for your flagship work (the deep-unrolled precoding), a detail
  page is where figures, results, and contributions live ‚ÄĒ a bare card can't
  show those, and committees value depth. Keep the option open.
  - Consequence: with Read More gone, the truncated abstract needs to expand 
  inline on click (a small "more" toggle in the card) rather than link out ‚ÄĒ so
  nothing is lost. Confirm that's what you want.

  4 & 5. Truncate + authors ‚ÄĒ good, no notes.

  Two small additions from my side

  - Type-pill vocabulary: I'll standardize labels ‚ÄĒ Conference Paper ¬∑ Journal 
  Paper ¬∑ Preprint ¬∑ Thesis ¬∑ Manuscript ‚ÄĒ derived from the bib entry so they
  stay consistent.
  - Section order: Publications first, then Ongoing Research. Honest and
  conventional, even while Publications is briefly light.

  Final confirms before I build

‚óŹ I read all four READMEs ‚ÄĒ this is excellent material, and a strong idea.
  Here's my evaluation.

  Verdict: yes, and it genuinely strengthens your profile

  These four are real, well-documented, hands-on builds:
  - Bluetooth-Controlled Car ‚ÄĒ 4WD Arduino, ultrasonic obstacle avoidance, web
  simulator.
  - Power System Fault Detection ‚ÄĒ an ML pipeline (RF detection 99.5%, NN
  classification, NN location regressor) on Simulink data.
  - IoT Smart Home ‚ÄĒ ESP8266, multi-sensor, 4-appliance relay control, OLED,
  ThingSpeak cloud.
  - IoT Smart Kitchen ‚ÄĒ ESP8266, gas-leak safety, motion lighting, live web
  dashboard.

  They show you can build hardware + ML + IoT systems end-to-end ‚ÄĒ exactly the
  practical counterweight to your (all-theoretical) research. Committees like
  seeing both. And unlike the old fake stock images, these have genuine result 
  figures (confusion matrices, dashboards, architecture diagrams).

  How I'd build it

  Data-driven, like the research page ‚ÄĒ each project is one Markdown file whose
  body auto-generates its detail page and feeds a card on the index. So the
  index loops your projects into cards (name + one-line description + Read More
  ‚Üí), and Read More opens that project's page. Adding a project later = one
  file. I'd copy the real images into the site and point the pages at them.

  Key suggestions

  1. Curate the detail pages ‚ÄĒ don't dump the raw README. Keep the overview,
  architecture, features, and result images; trim the exhaustive pin-wiring
  tables and code (too granular for a portfolio ‚ÄĒ link to GitHub for that). A
  portfolio page should sell the project, not document it.
  2. Cards text-only (matching the research page) is my default ‚ÄĒ but since you
  have real figures, a small thumbnail per card is a genuine option here. Your
  call.
  3. Link the GitHub repo on each detail page if these are public ‚ÄĒ reviewers
  love clicking into real code.

  build Undergraduate now and leave Self-Projects for when you have content (I
  won't show an empty section), or do you have self-project content to include

  "Self-Projects," but your call.)
  2. Scope of Undergraduate: just these 4 folder projects? Your CV also lists
  Speech/Voice Attendance, Gesture Wheelchair, FPGA Fan Control ‚ÄĒ add those as
  extra (lighter, no detail page), or leave them off?
  3. Detail pages: curated (my rec) or the full README verbatim?
  4. Cards: text-only (rec) or with a real-image thumbnail?
  5. GitHub: are these repos public? If so, paste the URL(s) and I'll link them.
  6. Confirm I should remove the old research _projects (deep-unrolled, hybrid,

‚óŹ Both posts are live on the blog (now 4 cards). Refresh /blog/.

  Post 1 ‚ÄĒ "Thinking right is the right thinking" (730 words): synthesizes all
  five books around the shared thread that the obvious answer is usually wrong.
  It pairs Kahneman and Dobelli as the same diagnosis at different altitudes
  (mechanism vs. field-guide), brings in Grant's "rethink / think like a
  scientist," then the "both versions can be true" turn ‚ÄĒ Ridley reframing the
  mind's biases as evolved features (a bug in a spreadsheet, a feature on the
  savanna), and Diamond rejecting the flattering story for geography (with his
  own critics showing even that needs rethinking).

  Post 2 ‚ÄĒ "Again and Again and Again‚Ä¶.." (733 words): the habit loop (Duhigg's
  cue-routine-reward, Clear's added craving + compounding/keystone habits), the
  psychology (you are what you repeat; willpower runs out), then Newport's Deep
  Work ‚ÄĒ "work = time √ó intensity of focus" ‚ÄĒ argued as itself a habit (rituals
  = cues + routines), closing the chain: habits free attention ‚Üí deep work 
  spends it ‚Üí output compounds into success.

  Both are grounded strictly in what the books actually argue (I verified each
  thesis from multiple summaries/reviews first), written in the same human,
  first-person essay voice as your earlier posts, and filed under Book review.

  Key sources I checked: The Red Queen (Wikipedia) (https://en.wikipedia.org/wik
  i/The_Red_Queen:_Sex_and_the_Evolution_of_Human_Nature) ¬∑ Guns, Germs, and
  Steel (Britannica) (https://www.britannica.com/question/What-is-the-main-argum
  ent-of-Guns-Germs-and-Steel) ¬∑ Think Again (SparkNotes)
  (https://www.sparknotes.com/lit/think-again/summary-and-analysis/) ¬∑ The Art
  of Thinking Clearly (SuperSummary)
  (https://www.supersummary.com/the-art-of-thinking-clearly/summary/) ¬∑ Atomic
  Habits vs Power of Habit
  (https://bookreadingtips.com/atomic-habits-vs-the-power-of-habit/) ¬∑ Deep Work
  (grahammann.net) (https://grahammann.net/book-notes/deep-work-cal-newport).

       5  description: What three books on habit and focus reveal about r
          epetition, attention, and the quiet machinery behind success.
       6  tags: habits productivity focus
       7  categories: [book review]
       8 +thumbnail: assets/img/blog/again-and-again.jpg                 
       9  ---
      10  
      11 +<img src="/assets/img/blog/again-and-again.jpg" alt="A habit tr
         +acker filled in week by week" class="img-fluid rounded z-depth-
         +1" style="max-width: 380px; display: block; margin: 0 auto 1.75
         +rem;">                                                         
      12 +                                                               
      13  The title of this post is a joke I stole from my own to-do list
          . For years the same three or four items just kept reappearing.
           Learn this. Finish that. Focus. I used to read the repetition 
          as failure. Three books ‚ÄĒ James Clear's *Atomic Habits*, Charle
          s Duhigg's *The Power of Habit*, and Cal Newport's *Deep Work* 
          ‚ÄĒ slowly convinced me it was the opposite. The repetition wasn'
          t the problem. It was the entire mechanism.
      14  
      15  Start with the machinery. Duhigg's central idea is that a habit
           is a loop with three parts: a cue that triggers it, a routine 
          you run, and a reward that makes the loop worth repeating. Do i
          t often enough and the brain stops deliberating ‚ÄĒ it hands the 
          whole sequence to autopilot to save energy. Clear keeps the loo
          p but sharpens it, slipping a fourth piece into the middle: cra
          ving. The cue doesn't just start the routine; it starts a wanti
          ng, and the wanting is the engine. It is the same diagram drawn
           at higher resolution, and the extra piece matters, because cra
          ving is where a habit is actually won or lost.

      12 +                                                               
      13  For a while I went on a strange reading run ‚ÄĒ five books that, 
          on paper, have almost nothing to do with each other. Two are ab
          out the wiring of the human mind. One is about how to change it
          . One is about sex and evolution. One is about why some societi
          es ended up conquering others. I did not plan it as a course in
           anything. But somewhere in the middle I noticed they were all 
          quietly telling the same uncomfortable story.
      14  
      15  The story is this: the answer that feels obvious is usually the
           wrong one, and thinking well is mostly the work of distrusting
           it.
